    \section{Data Wrangling (WeRateDogs
Data)}\label{data-wrangling-weratedogs-data}

\begin{figure}
\centering
\includegraphics{https://d17h27t6h515a5.cloudfront.net/topher/2017/October/59dd378f_dog-rates-social/dog-rates-social.jpg}
\caption{Image via Boston Magazine}
\end{figure}

\subsection{Table of Contents}\label{table-of-contents}

Introduction

Gathering

Assessing

Cleaning

Iterating

Storing

Acting

Conclusion

References

     \#\# Introduction

 WeRateDogs is a Twitter account that rates people's dogs with a
humorous comment about the dog. Their Twitter account data as many other
real world cases does not comes clean, so as part of the Udacity's Data
Analyst Nanodegree program the data wrangling process must be applied in
order to obtain data that will be useful to create interesting and
trustworthy analyses and visualizations of these rates.

\subsubsection{Objectives}\label{objectives}

\begin{itemize}
\item
  Gathering: Gather data from three different sources in order to create
  a master dataset \textbf{(WeRateDogs Twitter archive, Image
  predictions file and Twitter API)}.
\item
  Assessing: Assess both visually and programmatically for quality and
  tidiness issues. Detect and document at least \textbf{8 quality issues
  and 2 tidiness issues}.
\item
  Cleaning: Clean each of the issues you documented while assessing.
  \textbf{The result should be a high quality and tidy master pandas
  DataFrame (or DataFrames, if appropriate)}.
\item
  Storing: Store the clean DataFrame(s) in a CSV file with the main one.
  \textbf{Additionally, store the cleaned data in an SQLite database}.
\item
  Acting: Analyze and visualize the wrangled data, \textbf{producing at
  least 3 insights and 1 visualization}.
\end{itemize}

     \#\# Gathering the Data

The first source that will be gather is the WeRateDogs Twitter archive,
this file has been downloaded manually from the following url:
\href{https://d17h27t6h515a5.cloudfront.net/topher/2017/August/59a4e958_twitter-archive-enhanced/twitter-archive-enhanced.csv}{Data
source 1}.

After the download, I transferred the file to the * src * folder located
in the main directory of this notebook. Once there we read the file
using the \texttt{read\_csv} function from Pandas.

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
{\color{incolor}In [{\color{incolor}7}]:} \PY{n}{folder\PYZus{}name} \PY{o}{=} \PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{src}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}
        \PY{n}{twitter\PYZus{}archive} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{pd}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{read\PYZus{}csv}\PY{p}{(}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{src/twitter\PYZhy{}archive\PYZhy{}enhanced\PYZhy{}2.csv}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{)}
        \PY{n}{twitter\PYZus{}archive}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{head}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{)}
\end{Verbatim}


\begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]

    \begin{quote}

\end{quote}

     \#\# Assesing Data

    \subsubsection{Visual Assessment}\label{visual-assessment}

The very first step when assessing the data is to do it visually, even
though this might not be effective for large datasets, it will help us
to get acquainted with the data.

\paragraph{Twitter Archive Dataset}\label{twitter-archive-dataset}

    \begin{quote}
Indentified issues: - Missing values for columns:
(retweeted\_status\_id, retweeted\_status\_user\_id,
retweeted\_status\_timestamp, in\_reply\_to\_status\_id,
in\_reply\_to\_user\_id). - There is no information about the type of
dog, 'None' value for columns: (doggo, floofer, pupper, puppo). -
\texttt{source} column has embedded HTML code.
\end{quote}

    \texttt{twitter\_archive} columns: - \textbf{tweet\_id}: is the tweet
identifier. - \textbf{in\_reply\_to\_status\_id}: reply status
identifier. - \textbf{in\_reply\_to\_user\_id}: reply to user
identifier. - \textbf{timestamp} the timestamp assigned to each tweet
when it is created. - \textbf{source}: the source (mobile) from which
the tweet was made. - \textbf{text}: the text (body) that each tweet has
(during that time Twitter only allowed texts of 140 characters max). -
\textbf{retweeted\_status\_id}: identifier of the status if this tweet
was retweeted. - \textbf{retweeted\_status\_user\_id}: identifier of the
user if this tweet was retweeted. -
\textbf{retweeted\_status\_timestamp}: the timestamp given if this tweet
was retweeted. - \textbf{expanded\_urls}: expanded urls. -
\textbf{rating\_numerator}: numerator of the ranking, almost always
above 10. - \textbf{rating\_denominator}: denominator of the ranking,
fixed to 10. - \textbf{name}: the given name to the dog. -
\textbf{doggo}: a type of dog. A big pupper, usually older. This label
does not stop a doggo from behaving like a pupper. - \textbf{floofer}: a
type of dog. A any dog really. However, this label is commonly given to
dogs with semmingly excess fur. - \textbf{pupper}: a type of dog. A
small doggo, usually younger. Can be equally, if not more mature than
some doggos. - \textbf{puppo}: a type of dog. A transitional state
between pupper and doggo. Easily understood as the dog equivalent of a
teenager.

\textbf{Definitions for dogs were taken from:} \emph{TheDogtionary (via
the \#WeRateDogs book on Amazon)}

\end{Verbatim}

    \begin{quote}
Indentified issues: - Some breeds are capitalized while others not, also
instead of a space the character '\_' is used, for columns: (p1, p2, p3)
\end{quote}

    \texttt{image\_predictions} columns: - \textbf{tweet\_id}: is the tweet
identifier. - \textbf{jpg\_url}: the url to the image of the dog used
for the prediction. - \textbf{img\_num}: number of image. - \textbf{p1}:
p1 is the algorithm's \#1 prediction for the image in the tweet. -
\textbf{p1\_conf}: p1\_conf is how confident the algorithm is in its \#1
prediction. - \textbf{p1\_dog}: p1\_dog is whether or not the \#1
prediction is a breed of dog. - \textbf{p2}: p2 is the algorithm's
second most likely prediction. - \textbf{p2\_conf}: p2\_conf is how
confident the algorithm is in its \#2 prediction. - \textbf{p2\_dog}:
p2\_dog is whether or not the \#2 prediction is a breed of dog. -
\textbf{p3}: p3 is the algorithm's third most likely prediction. -
\textbf{p3\_conf}: p2\_conf is how confident the algorithm is in its \#3
prediction. - \textbf{p3\_dog}: p2\_dog is whether or not the \#3
prediction is a breed of dog.

    \texttt{tweets\_counts} columns: - \textbf{tweet\_id}: is the tweet
identifier. - \textbf{retweet\_count}: number of retweets of that tweet.
- \textbf{favorite\_count}: number of favourites of that tweet.

datasets, using pandas functions. \#\#\#\# Twitter Archive

{\color{incolor}In [{\color{incolor}27}]:} \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Both numerator and denominator seem to be pretty high, lets look at the text to see why.}
         \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Something seems odd about text and the numerators, leets look at them}

  Tweet: (832088576586297345) - Invalid rating

  2 or more dogs. Tweets: (820690176645140481, 713900603437621249,
  710658690886586372, 709198395643068416, 704054845121142784,

    \textbf{Looking at these tweets we realize something pretty funny about
all of them, the one with 1776/10 makes reference to the independence
year of USA, the one with 666 makes reference to the "number of the
devil"}

    \begin{quote}
Since they are special cases, we might consider to remove them, or do
not take them into account for further analysis. Tweets:
(855862651834028034, 855860136149123072, 749981277374128128,
670842764863651840)
\end{quote}

\end{quote}

    \subsubsection{Observations}\label{observations}

\paragraph{Quality}\label{quality}

\texttt{twitter\_achive\ table} - There are rows that belong to
retweets, we should get rid of this rows. - These columns are not needed
since they belong to retweets: (retweeted\_status\_id,
retweeted\_status\_user\_id, retweeted\_status\_timestamp,
in\_reply\_to\_status\_id, in\_reply\_to\_user\_id).

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  In the name column, the name is not an actual name. There are serveral
  prepositions that shouldn't be there, like: "the, an, this, etc".
\item
  Incorrect datatype for the column 'timestamp', instead of string it
  should be datetime.
\item
  Incorrect value for the columns \emph{(doggo, floofer, pupper, puppo)}
  they should have nan instead of 'None'.
\item
  The rate assigned to the following tweets is incorrect, they should be
  corrected. Tweets (835246439529840640, 666287406224695296,
  775096608509886464, 740373189193256964, 716439118184652801,
  682962037429899265, 722974582966214656) {[}14/10, 14/10, 11/10, 10/10,
  13/10, 13/10, 9/10{]} - Incorrect rating
\item
  The rate assigned to the following tweets is for all the dogs that
  appear on it, so the values should be recalculated. Tweets
  (758467244762497024, 731156023742988288, 684225744407494656,
  684222868335505415, 677716515794329600, 820690176645140481,
  713900603437621249, 710658690886586372, 709198395643068416,
  704054845121142784, 697463031882764288, 675853064436391936) - Adjust
  rating
\item
  These tweets do not have valid ratings and there is no futher
  information that we can use, so they should be removed. Tweets
  (810984652412424192, 855862651834028034, 855860136149123072,
  749981277374128128, 670842764863651840 )
\end{itemize}

\texttt{image\_predictions\ table} - Columns: \emph{(p1, p1\_conf,
p1\_dog, p2, p2\_conf, p2\_dog, p3, p3\_conf, p3\_dog)} are not
informative enough. - In the columns \emph{(p1, p2, p3)} all the values
should be converted to lower case to avoid misspelling.

\paragraph{Tidiness}\label{tidiness}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  There are 2075 rows in \texttt{image\_prediction\ table}, 2356 in
  \texttt{tweet\_archive\ table}, and 2354
  \texttt{tweets\_count\ table}.
\item
  The types of dog corresponds to only one variable which is called the
  age stage of that dog.
\item
  At the end we only need 1 a table that contains all the data relevant
  for our analysis (observational unit).
\item
  In \texttt{image\_prediction\ table} we only need 1 column for the
  breed and the result, instead of the 3.
\end{itemize}

     \#\# Cleaning Data

    \paragraph{Making a copy of the three
datasets}\label{making-a-copy-of-the-three-datasets}

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]

    \subsubsection{Missing Data}\label{missing-data}

\texttt{twitter\_archivecp}

\paragraph{Define}\label{define}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Remove all the rows that belong to retweets.
\item
  Remove columns that are associated with retweets
  (retweeted\_status\_id, retweeted\_status\_user\_id,
  retweeted\_status\_timestamp, in\_reply\_to\_status\_id,
  in\_reply\_to\_user\_id).
\item
  Remove all the rows that contain tweets that have no valid ratings:
  (810984652412424192, 855862651834028034, 855860136149123072,
  749981277374128128, 670842764863651840 )
\end{itemize}

    \paragraph{Code}\label{code}

    \paragraph{Define}\label{define}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Recalculate and correct the ratings for the following tweets:
  (758467244762497024, 731156023742988288, 684225744407494656,
  684222868335505415, 677716515794329600, 820690176645140481,
  713900603437621249, 710658690886586372, 709198395643068416,
  704054845121142784, 697463031882764288, 675853064436391936)
\end{itemize}

\end{Verbatim}
            
    \paragraph{Define}\label{define}

\texttt{image\_predictions\ table} - Convert values of columns
(p1,p2,p3) to lowercase - Rename the columns (p1, p1\_conf, p1\_dog, p2,
p2\_conf, p2\_dog, p3, p3\_conf, p3\_dog) to (prediction\_\#,
conf\_probability\_\#, predicted\_breed\_\#), where \# is the number 1,2
and 3. - Create two columns (breed, result) were the values with the
highest probability will be held.

    \paragraph{Code}\label{code}

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
{\color{incolor}In [{\color{incolor}68}]:} \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} We convert the columns \PYZsq{}p1\PYZsq{}, \PYZsq{}p2\PYZsq{} and \PYZsq{}p3\PYZsq{} to lowercase}
         \PY{n}{columns} \PY{o}{=} \PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{p1}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{p2}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{p3}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{]}
         \PY{k}{for} \PY{n}{column} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{n}{columns}\PY{p}{:}
             \PY{n}{image\PYZus{}predictions\PYZus{}copy}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{column}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{image\PYZus{}predictions\PYZus{}copy}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{column}\PY{p}{]}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{str}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{lower}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{)}
\end{Verbatim}


    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
{\color{incolor}In [{\color{incolor}69}]:} \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Now we rename the columns (p1, p1\PYZus{}conf, p1\PYZus{}dog, p2, p2\PYZus{}conf, p2\PYZus{}dog, p3, p3\PYZus{}conf, p3\PYZus{}dog)}
         \PY{n}{image\PYZus{}predictions\PYZus{}copy}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{rename}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{columns}\PY{o}{=}\PY{p}{\PYZob{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{p1}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{:} \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{prediction\PYZus{}1}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{p2}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{:} \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{prediction:\PYZus{}2}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{p3}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{:} \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{prediction:\PYZus{}3}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{,} 
                                             \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{p1\PYZus{}conf}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{:} \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{conf\PYZus{}probability\PYZus{}1}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{p2\PYZus{}conf}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{:} \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{conf\PYZus{}probability\PYZus{}2}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{,} 
                                             \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{p3\PYZus{}conf}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{:} \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{conf\PYZus{}probability\PYZus{}3}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{p1\PYZus{}dog}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{:} \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{predicted\PYZus{}breed\PYZus{}1}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{,}
                                             \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{p2\PYZus{}dog}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{:} \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{predicted\PYZus{}breed\PYZus{}2}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{p3\PYZus{}dog}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{:} \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{predicted\PYZus{}breed\PYZus{}3}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{,}\PY{p}{\PYZcb{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{inplace}\PY{o}{=}\PY{k+kc}{True}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{;}
\end{Verbatim}


    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
{\color{incolor}In [{\color{incolor}70}]:} \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} We add a new column in which we will save the breed (in case of a dog) or object with the highest probaility}
         \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} and another column which states that if it is a dog or not.}
         \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Remove all the rows in which neither of the 3 predictions are dogs}
         \PY{n}{indexes} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{image\PYZus{}predictions\PYZus{}copy}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{index}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{image\PYZus{}predictions\PYZus{}copy}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{predicted\PYZus{}breed\PYZus{}1}\PY{p}{)} \PY{o}{|} 
                             \PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{image\PYZus{}predictions\PYZus{}copy}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{predicted\PYZus{}breed\PYZus{}2}\PY{p}{)} \PY{o}{|} 
                             \PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{image\PYZus{}predictions\PYZus{}copy}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{predicted\PYZus{}breed\PYZus{}3}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{)} \PY{o}{==} \PY{k+kc}{False}\PY{p}{]}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{tolist}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{)}
         
         
         \PY{n+nb}{len}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{indexes}\PY{p}{)}
\end{Verbatim}


\begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
{\color{outcolor}Out[{\color{outcolor}70}]:} 324
\end{Verbatim}
            
    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]

         \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Now lets look at duplicated urls}
         \PY{n}{indexes} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{image\PYZus{}predictions\PYZus{}copy}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{image\PYZus{}predictions\PYZus{}copy}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{jpg\PYZus{}url}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{duplicated}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{keep} \PY{o}{=} \PY{k+kc}{False}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{]}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{sort\PYZus{}values}\PY{p}{(}
             \PY{n}{by} \PY{o}{=} \PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{jpg\PYZus{}url}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{)}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{index}
         \PY{n+nb}{len}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{indexes}\PY{p}{)}
\end{Verbatim}

    \begin{quote}
Reading at the text we notice that the problem was that the numerators
are the decimal values of the rates.

    \subsubsection{Quality}\label{quality}

\texttt{twitter\_archive\_copy} - The rate assigned to the following
tweets is incorrect, they should be corrected. Tweets:
(786709082849828864, 778027034220126208, 680494726643068929) {[}10/10,
11/10, 11/10{]}

    \subsection{Cleaning}\label{cleaning}

    \paragraph{Define}\label{define}

Correct the ratings for the following tweets: (786709082849828864,
778027034220126208, 680494726643068929). Ratings: {[}10/10, 11/10,
11/10{]}.

    \paragraph{Code}\label{code}

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
{\color{incolor}In [{\color{incolor}77}]:} \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} For the ones who were not deleted we proceed to adjust the ratings}
         \PY{n}{adjust\PYZus{}tweets} \PY{o}{=} \PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{786709082849828864}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+m+mi}{778027034220126208}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+m+mi}{680494726643068929}\PY{p}{]}
         \PY{n}{ratings} \PY{o}{=} \PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{10}\PY{p}{,}\PY{l+m+mi}{10}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{,} \PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{11}\PY{p}{,}\PY{l+m+mi}{10}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{,} \PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{11}\PY{p}{,}\PY{l+m+mi}{10}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{]}
         \PY{n}{indexes} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{twitter\PYZus{}archive\PYZus{}copy}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{index}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{twitter\PYZus{}archive\PYZus{}copy}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{tweet\PYZus{}id}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{isin}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{adjust\PYZus{}tweets}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{]}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{tolist}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{)}
         \PY{n}{indexes}
\end{Verbatim}

    \subsubsection{Tidiness}\label{tidiness}

    \paragraph{Define}\label{define}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Group the different types of doggs into only one column named age
  stage which will contain all the stages of the dog's age.
\end{itemize}

    \paragraph{Code}\label{code}

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
{\color{incolor}In [{\color{incolor}80}]:} \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Map each stage of the dog that exists: doggo, floofer, puper, puppo}
         \PY{n}{age\PYZus{}stages} \PY{o}{=} \PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{doggo}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{floofer}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{pupper}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{puppo}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{]}
         \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Function that maps every state of the dogs}
         \PY{k}{def} \PY{n+nf}{calc\PYZus{}dog\PYZus{}stage}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{stages}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}
             \PY{k}{for} \PY{n}{stage} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{n}{stages}\PY{p}{:}
                 \PY{k}{if} \PY{n}{stage} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{n}{age\PYZus{}stages}\PY{p}{:}
                     \PY{k}{return} \PY{n}{stage}
                 \PY{k}{else}\PY{p}{:}
                     \PY{k}{pass}
             \PY{k}{return} \PY{n}{stage}
\end{Verbatim}


    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
{\color{incolor}In [{\color{incolor}81}]:} \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Apply the given function}
         \PY{n}{twitter\PYZus{}archive\PYZus{}copy}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{age\PYZus{}stages}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{twitter\PYZus{}archive\PYZus{}copy}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{doggo}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{floofer}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{,}  \PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{pupper}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{puppo}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{]}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{apply}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{calc\PYZus{}dog\PYZus{}stage}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{axis} \PY{o}{=} \PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{)}
         \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Then we drop the remaining columns}
         \PY{n}{twitter\PYZus{}archive\PYZus{}copy}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{drop}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{doggo}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{floofer}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{pupper}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{puppo}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{,} 
             \PY{n}{inplace} \PY{o}{=} \PY{k+kc}{True}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{axis} \PY{o}{=} \PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{)}
         \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Finally we convert that variable as category}
         \PY{n}{twitter\PYZus{}archive\PYZus{}copy}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{age\PYZus{}stages} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{twitter\PYZus{}archive\PYZus{}copy}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{age\PYZus{}stages}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{astype}\PY{p}{(}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{category}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{)}
\end{Verbatim}


    \paragraph{Test}\label{test}

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]

    \paragraph{Define}\label{define}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  In \texttt{image\_prediction\ table} create two arrays one with the
  prediction, and other with the result of the predictions that had the
  highest probability.
\end{itemize}

    \paragraph{Code}\label{code}

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
{\color{incolor}In [{\color{incolor}84}]:} \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} We create a two list, one with the object and other with the result}
         \PY{n}{predictions} \PY{o}{=} \PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{]}
         \PY{n}{results} \PY{o}{=} \PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{]}
         
         \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} For loop, were the values with the highest probability are selected and appended}
         \PY{k}{for} \PY{n}{i} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{n+nb}{range} \PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{image\PYZus{}predictions\PYZus{}copy}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{shape}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}
             \PY{n}{prob1} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{image\PYZus{}predictions\PYZus{}copy}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{loc}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{i}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{conf\PYZus{}probability\PYZus{}1}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{]}
             \PY{n}{prob2} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{image\PYZus{}predictions\PYZus{}copy}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{loc}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{i}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{conf\PYZus{}probability\PYZus{}2}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{]}
             \PY{n}{prob3} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{image\PYZus{}predictions\PYZus{}copy}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{loc}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{i}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{conf\PYZus{}probability\PYZus{}3}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{]}
             
             \PY{k}{if} \PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{prob1} \PY{o}{\PYZgt{}} \PY{n}{prob2}\PY{p}{)} \PY{o+ow}{and} \PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{prob1} \PY{o}{\PYZgt{}} \PY{n}{prob3}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}
                 \PY{n}{predictions}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{append}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{image\PYZus{}predictions\PYZus{}copy}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{loc}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{i}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{prediction\PYZus{}1}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{)}
                 \PY{n}{results}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{append}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{image\PYZus{}predictions\PYZus{}copy}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{loc}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{i}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{predicted\PYZus{}breed\PYZus{}1}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{)}
             \PY{k}{elif} \PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{prob2} \PY{o}{\PYZgt{}} \PY{n}{prob1}\PY{p}{)} \PY{o+ow}{and} \PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{prob2} \PY{o}{\PYZgt{}} \PY{n}{prob3}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}
                 \PY{n}{predictions}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{append}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{image\PYZus{}predictions\PYZus{}copy}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{loc}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{i}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{prediction\PYZus{}2}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{)}
                 \PY{n}{results}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{append}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{image\PYZus{}predictions\PYZus{}copy}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{loc}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{i}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{predicted\PYZus{}breed\PYZus{}2}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{)}
             \PY{k}{else}\PY{p}{:}
                 \PY{n}{predictions}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{append}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{image\PYZus{}predictions\PYZus{}copy}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{loc}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{i}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{prediction\PYZus{}3}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{)}
                 \PY{n}{results}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{append}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{image\PYZus{}predictions\PYZus{}copy}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{loc}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{i}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{predicted\PYZus{}breed\PYZus{}3}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{)}
\end{Verbatim}

    \paragraph{Define}\label{define}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Combine the 3 tables together into a single table named:
  \texttt{twitter\_archive\_master.csv}.
\item
  Drop the columns that will be not part of the analysis.
\end{itemize}

    \paragraph{Code}\label{code}

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]

     \#\# Store the data

Finally we have our dataset cleaned and ready to be stored, we will use
SQL Lite as DBMS to create a database and store
\texttt{twitter\_archive\ table}.

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]

    \subsubsection{Questions}\label{questions}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  is there any relation between the number of retweets and favorites
  variables?
\item
  What's the distribution that follows both retweet count and favorite
  count?
\item
  Does the age states of a dog have anything to do with the rating?
\item
  What kind of breeds of dogs do the followers retweet and favorite
  more?
\item
  Does certain breeds of dogs have better rating than others?
\item
  Which are the top 10 names for dogs.
\end{itemize}

    \paragraph{Is there any relation between the number of retweets and
favorites
variables?}\label{is-there-any-relation-between-the-number-of-retweets-and-favorites-variables}

\begin{quote}
From here we calculate the correlation for all the numeric variables.
\end{quote}

    \paragraph{Does certain breeds of dogs have better rating than
others?}\label{does-certain-breeds-of-dogs-have-better-rating-than-others}

\begin{quote}
Note: We can repeat the process used for the previous graph, just that
this time we obtain the mean instead of the sum.
\end{quote}

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
{\color{incolor}In [{\color{incolor}107}]:} \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Select only those instances that correspond to actual images of dogs, not objects or other stuff}
          \PY{n}{top\PYZus{}ratings} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{twitter\PYZus{}archive\PYZus{}master}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{twitter\PYZus{}archive\PYZus{}master}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{results} \PY{o}{==} \PY{k+kc}{True}\PY{p}{]}
          \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Group by the breed (predictions), obtain the mean, and reset their index}
          \PY{n}{top\PYZus{}ratings} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{top\PYZus{}ratings}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{groupby}\PY{p}{(}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{predictions}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{)}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{mean}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{)}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{reset\PYZus{}index}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{)}
          \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Select the predictions and rating\PYZus{}numerator variables}
          \PY{n}{top\PYZus{}ratings} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{top\PYZus{}ratings}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{predictions}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{rating\PYZus{}numerator}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{]}
          \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} We select only the top 20 breeds of dogs}
          \PY{n}{top\PYZus{}ratings} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{top\PYZus{}ratings}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{sort\PYZus{}values}\PY{p}{(}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{rating\PYZus{}numerator}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{ascending} \PY{o}{=} \PY{k+kc}{False}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{:}\PY{l+m+mi}{20}\PY{p}{]}

     \#\# Conclusions \#\#\# Limitations - The datasets that were wrangled
they required an extensive assesing in order to be completly cleanded.
so for the purpose of this excercise I limitated to assess and clean one
variable for further analysis. - The final dataset can offer multiple
analysis and insights thanks to the amount of data and feature
engineering, though only univariate and bivariate analysis were made,
leaving outside the possible insights that multivariate visualization
could have offered. - In case that the amount of information increases,
some techniques like the one I used for checking the outliers might
become unfeasible, so the use of technologies like \emph{Natural
Language Processing} in text analysis become a need.

    \subsubsection{Summary}\label{summary}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Golden retriever and labrador are very popular breeds of dogs,
  surprisingly that doesn't necessarily mean that they have a good
  rating (As it was expected).
\item
  There is an almost equitative quatity for the most popular names for
  girls and boys (dogs).
\item
  We rate dogs in average gives pretty similar rates no matter the age
  of the dogs (with very slightly differences).
\item
  As in most of the trends and popular posts, the number of favorites
  and retweets of WeRateDogs are correlated.
\end{itemize}

     \#\# References - \textbf{Seaborn Pydata:
https://seaborn.pydata.org/examples/many\_pairwise\_correlations.html} -
\textbf{Matplotlib: https://plot.ly/matplotlib/bar-charts/}
